  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7b762d18-20fb-4531-bfb2-0f2bcc4fc343'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4658970917322609233">Are you ready for the 88-page long epic graphic novel inspired by the most famous historic last stand?<br/><br/><b>Ahoo Ahoo Ahoo</b><br/><i>(I hope everyone here chanted that with me)</i><br/><br/><blockquote>

  <span id="freeText4658970917322609233" style="display:none">Are you ready for the 88-page long epic graphic novel inspired by the most famous historic last stand?<br><br><b>Ahoo Ahoo Ahoo</b><br><i>(I hope everyone here chanted that with me)</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Into the hell's mouth..... we march.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495011578i/22775348._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Set in 480 BC, Frank Miller's 300 retells the battle of Thermopylae: a battle that raged between 300 Spartans and allied forces against the full strength of Persian army. <br><br><i>And what a battle it was.</i><br><br>This limited graphic series is considered as one of the most acclaimed works of Frank Miller. You'd know why that particular opinion persists when you read this book. The story is so well written and you could actually feel the energy flowing through the words when you read the story. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495011578i/22775349.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The art is also beautiful in many panels. But some were just average for me.<br><br>We all love the movie 300. And now I can state confidently that the movie is one hell of an adaptation of its source material. The movie not only absorbs the story faithfully but also manages to transcend the source material in many parts.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495011578i/22775350._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466838882ra/19523552.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Overall, if you are looking for something energetic... Read this book!<br><br>Once again, together now!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495011578ra/22775351.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1759537691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1759537691" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1759537691?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18892304-300">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759537691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12099606066972723819">As with many comics and graphic novels, I've seen the movie before I read the book. But despite the extreme pathos, the floods of blood / body parts and the ridiculous make-up/CGI abs, I liked it. Thus I wanted to read the graphic novel.<br/><br/>The book is pretty short but it also has just the right length. It's not historically accurate, but I also didn't expect that since its purpose rather is to entertain, shock (corpses! nudity!) and give a new coating to an already very well-known point in history.</span>
  <span id="freeText12099606066972723819" style="display:none">As with many comics and graphic novels, I've seen the movie before I read the book. But despite the extreme pathos, the floods of blood / body parts and the ridiculous make-up/CGI abs, I liked it. Thus I wanted to read the graphic novel.<br><br>The book is pretty short but it also has just the right length. It's not historically accurate, but I also didn't expect that since its purpose rather is to entertain, shock (corpses! nudity!) and give a new coating to an already very well-known point in history.<br><br>The art in this is gritty but beautiful. Before seeing the movie, I hadn't seen this style before what with the brownish colours everywhere and bright red as a shock - alas, since then many have copied it, but this will always be the first and therefore original to me. <br><br>There was little enough dialogue. Instead, we are being told a story, a tale as told by the one Spartan who was sent back and I can imagine telling this tale around a campfire. That was a rather nice touch as well. Plus, the book had (as I had hoped) my two favourite scenes in it:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474036218i/20546146.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474036218i/20546147._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So yeah, despite the historical inaccuracies and the thick coat of pathos everywhere, I enjoyed myself very much and understand why Frank Miller's work usually gets a lot of praise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12099606066972723819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5040162173489362715" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>"Persians gasp and groan and gurgle and scream and stumble and tumble and fall. Brains splattering across briny stone . . . We Spartans laugh like fools - and keep pushing. <b>No prisoners. No mercy.</b> We're off to one hell of a good start."</i> -- King Leonides commenting on 'The First Day'<br /><br />Powerfully lean and mean - just like the warriors of the title - graphic novella epic (is that even a thing?) that is hyper-violent but also ruggedly stylish. Leonides and his trusted Spartan battalion are all that stand in the way of the waves of military forces invading the enlightened ancient nation of Greece. Lots of crazy warfare scenes (more severed limbs and appendages than you can throw a javelin at) along with terse but well-written dialogue = a tour-de-force from the talented Mr. Miller.</span>

  <i>Spartans! Tonight we dine in hell</i>

  <span id="freeText7844786667566071329" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Spartans! Tonight we dine in hell</i>
</b><br />The original graphic novel that inpired the movie of the same name. <br /><br />Graphics are amazing, unique and pioneer for their time; too brutal and too tale-like. Lines are as spartan-like as they should be: "το λακωνίζειν εστί φιλοσοφείν" (talk as less as you can to be wise) is the moto of these soldiers that fear nothing, even death himself. "Η ταν ή επί τας" (come carrying this shield or be brought up to it") is the other hesitate-in-front-of-no-enemy moto. <br /><br />Spartans and their sacrifice still inspires in many forms of art (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kF_nYCnVjcM">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kF_nY...</a>). The graphic novel itself inspired cinematography for a new animation-like CGI (like Spartakos)</span>

    <a title="Mario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16628840-mario"><img alt="Mario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588674821p2/16628840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1180820674?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180820674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8603897374414808564"><i>I prefer to die on my feet,than live on my knees.</i><br/><br/><br/>Ever since I've seen the movie adaptation of <i>300</i> (LONG time ago), I've been wanting to read the graphic novel, and now I finally got a chance to read it. I loved the movie adaptation of this (I even liked the sequel), and now that I finally read the graphic novel, I can safely say that I loved the graphic novel as well. I loved the art style, the way the story was told, and of course the characters. But I have to say, even though I loved the graph</span>
  <span id="freeText8603897374414808564" style="display:none"><i>I prefer to die on my feet,than live on my knees.</i><br /><br /><br />Ever since I've seen the movie adaptation of <i>300</i> (LONG time ago), I've been wanting to read the graphic novel, and now I finally got a chance to read it. I loved the movie adaptation of this (I even liked the sequel), and now that I finally read the graphic novel, I can safely say that I loved the graphic novel as well. I loved the art style, the way the story was told, and of course the characters. But I have to say, even though I loved the graphic novel, I still like the movie a bit more. The reason for that is probably because every single bit of the graphic novel was in a movie, but the movie just expanded the story more. Sometimes that can be a bad thing, but here it made the story deeper and more awesome. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_223941578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223941578" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223941578?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223941578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8576898503025791308">Though I'm a Frank Miller fan, back in 2006 I somehow hadn't heard of his book "300" so I went to see Zack Snyder's film first - and it completely blew me away. Maybe because I hadn't read Miller's book or seen anything about the film beforehand, but the film was shot in such a highly stylised way and the story was so utterly engrossing, that I couldn't get it out of my head and is probably one of my favourite films ever. Needless to say once I found out it was based on Miller's book I sought it</span>
  <span id="freeText8576898503025791308" style="display:none">Though I'm a Frank Miller fan, back in 2006 I somehow hadn't heard of his book "300" so I went to see Zack Snyder's film first - and it completely blew me away. Maybe because I hadn't read Miller's book or seen anything about the film beforehand, but the film was shot in such a highly stylised way and the story was so utterly engrossing, that I couldn't get it out of my head and is probably one of my favourite films ever. Needless to say once I found out it was based on Miller's book I sought it out and devoured it in one sitting. Years later I sat down with it again one rainy Saturday morning and after re-reading it I decided to set down my thoughts to encourage anyone out there reading this review who hasn't read this book to go out and read it now.<br /><br />The story is set in 480 BCE and is about King Leonidas of Sparta and 300 of his personal guard standing up to a massive Persian army many thousands strong led by the self-proclaimed god-king Xerxes. What looks like a massacre based on figures alone, changes when Leonidas chooses a narrow coastal passageway called the Hot Gates as the place he and his men will make their last stand. They will die but not without taking a fair chunk out of Xerxes' force, causing his army to stumble in their mission to dominate the civilised world, and inspire others to oppose and eventually defeat Xerxes. <br /><br />The story is ripe for drama and Miller milks it for all its worth, setting up each of the five chapters perfectly so that not a single panel is wasted. The dialogue is so memorable a lot of it was lifted straight from the book into the film: "This is blasphemy! This is madness!" - "This is SPARTA!", "Spartan! Come back with your shield - or on it", "Spartans. Ready your breakfast and eat hearty - for tonight we dine in Hell!" and so on. There are so many excellent passages like when the Spartans meet up with the Arcadians or Leonidas' confrontation with Xerxes that the words will ring through your mind long after you’ve read it (in my case years later).<br /><br />Then there's the art. If, like me, you were blown away by the visuals in the film, it's only because so many of the iconic scenes were taken straight from the book and Miller's imagination. Every page is a master-class in comics artistry from the night battle with the Immortals, to the dance of the Oracle, to the bottomless pit in Sparta, to Xerxes' character design, and the Spartans' iconic red cloaks, bronze shields and helmets. The book is printed on A4 pages with many panels taking up an entire page. Miller doesn't waste a single inch of space, filling it up with detail and action while his partner Lynn Varley elevates it with her colours to produce some of the most gorgeous art Miller has ever crafted in his career.<br /><br />"300" is an incredible accomplishment of art and storytelling and is one of the many reasons why Frank Miller is so revered in the literary world. It's as exhilarating to read on the page as it is to see on the screen and the art is to die for. I recommend this whole-heartedly to anyone who enjoys to read but especially to comics fans who've not picked this up yet. This is an amazing book, this is a work of art, THIS IS MILLER (at his finest)!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8576898503025791308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_662015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/662015" />
    <a title="Yi-Sheng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25429-yi-sheng"><img alt="Yi-Sheng" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/662015?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yi-Sheng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yi-Sheng" href="/user/show/25429-yi-sheng">Yi-Sheng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25429-yi-sheng?shelf=graphicnovels">graphicnovels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25429-yi-sheng?shelf=trash">trash</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6018557379542388538">Christ. This is crazy. Sparta's described as having this nightmarish culture where children are left out to die of exposure, men are ritually abused by each other to demonstrate toughness, the disabled are rejected in spite of their potential skills because they fail to fit into the military system, and international law is null and void (this is madness! No one kills a messenger! This is Sparta!).<br/><br/>And yet Frank Miller would have us believe they're better than the cultured Athenians (who're habit</span>
  <span id="freeText6018557379542388538" style="display:none">Christ. This is crazy. Sparta's described as having this nightmarish culture where children are left out to die of exposure, men are ritually abused by each other to demonstrate toughness, the disabled are rejected in spite of their potential skills because they fail to fit into the military system, and international law is null and void (this is madness! No one kills a messenger! This is Sparta!).<br /><br />And yet Frank Miller would have us believe they're better than the cultured Athenians (who're habitually described as boy-lovers, in spite of the Spartans being big macho maries themselves), that they can rationally reject their religion (the priests are painted as corrupt) and that what they're fighting for in their battle against the Persians is WESTERN CIVILISATION ITSELF.<br /><br />In the end, the invading Persians (who offer to enrich Sparta in exchange for her vassalship) sound a lot more like today's America. And the Spartans look a lot more like today's Iran, proud and smart enough to develop nuclear capability and cunning enough to abuse a few British sailors for the sake of political advantage.<br /><br />However, the stupid Americentric wankfest does read well. (shrug)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6018557379542388538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer63217485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1810808064337924753">The effort by Dark Horse Comics to make this hardcover edition of Frank Miller's 300 into a panoramic edition is appreciated. This was the way Miller intended as the individual issues (or floppies) were a 2 page splash from start to finish.<br/>My only gripe is I cannot display it spine first on my shelf with my other Miller works. But a great read nonetheless.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16702372986234092071">Zack Snyder's 2006 movie, 300 kept me on the edge of my seat as I watched it in the big screen. Until now, it still is one of my best guilty pleasure movies of all time. The slow motion choreography and the dumb macho rhetoric made me smile for days.<br/><br/>So, buying the 300 graphic novel by Frank Miller is the way to go to satiate my desire for more Spartan action. And man I am not disappointed. 300 has mindless fun and glorious deaths. The artwork is the best I have seen from Frank Miller.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485785604i/21846741._SX540_.jpg' width='600' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>300 the gra</span>
  <span id="freeText16702372986234092071" style="display:none">Zack Snyder's 2006 movie, 300 kept me on the edge of my seat as I watched it in the big screen. Until now, it still is one of my best guilty pleasure movies of all time. The slow motion choreography and the dumb macho rhetoric made me smile for days.<br><br>So, buying the 300 graphic novel by Frank Miller is the way to go to satiate my desire for more Spartan action. And man I am not disappointed. 300 has mindless fun and glorious deaths. The artwork is the best I have seen from Frank Miller.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485785604i/21846741._SX540_.jpg" width="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>300 the graphic novel holds the manliness record for the densest number spears, arrows, shields, red capes and abs in graphic literature.<br><br>I love 300 for what the satisfaction it gives from its mindless fun and glorious action.<br><br></span>

<div id="review_2138626043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2138626043" />
    <a title="Evan Leach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7713825-evan-leach"><img alt="Evan Leach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384621842p2/7713825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2138626043?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan Leach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan Leach" href="/user/show/7713825-evan-leach">Evan Leach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7713825-evan-leach?shelf=1990-1999">1990-1999</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7713825-evan-leach?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7713825-evan-leach?shelf=read-and-watched">read-and-watched</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2138626043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13134041347830146905"><i>300</i> offers a very cool reimagining of the Battle of Thermopylae. Like the famous movie adaptation, the book oozes style (I particularly enjoyed the exotic interpretation of the Persian Emperor and his armies), and the story is action packed and engaging. <br/><br/>This is not the deepest or most nuanced graphic novel I've ever read; it is the literary equivalent of an action movie. However, it succeeds on those terms very well. The artwork had some definite high points (creativity being #1), but personall</span>
  <span id="freeText13134041347830146905" style="display:none"><i>300</i> offers a very cool reimagining of the Battle of Thermopylae. Like the famous movie adaptation, the book oozes style (I particularly enjoyed the exotic interpretation of the Persian Emperor and his armies), and the story is action packed and engaging. <br /><br />This is not the deepest or most nuanced graphic novel I've ever read; it is the literary equivalent of an action movie. However, it succeeds on those terms very well. The artwork had some definite high points (creativity being #1), but personally I like Miller better as a storyteller than as an artist, and overall I found the art to be a mixed bag.<br /><br />A strong, exciting, fun read. <b>4.5 stars</b>, highly recommended!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13134041347830146905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1195235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195235" />
    <a title="J.G. Keely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely"><img alt="J.G. Keely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274333636p2/84023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195235?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.G. Keely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.G. Keely" href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely">J.G. Keely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1195235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1576924985058794731">Fun and exciting. A worthwhile story to be told, though the omission of the Thespians and other abuses of artistic license mark the fault of Miller's sensationalism. Like the four-color comics before him, Miller takes archetypes and symbols and drives them full throttle to the epic, gun-blazing climax. Unfortunately, character and emotion suffer. This is not quite the liability that it could have been, as the Epic tradition is often purposefully guilty of the same and 300 fits into this traditio</span>
  <span id="freeText1576924985058794731" style="display:none">Fun and exciting. A worthwhile story to be told, though the omission of the Thespians and other abuses of artistic license mark the fault of Miller's sensationalism. Like the four-color comics before him, Miller takes archetypes and symbols and drives them full throttle to the epic, gun-blazing climax. Unfortunately, character and emotion suffer. This is not quite the liability that it could have been, as the Epic tradition is often purposefully guilty of the same and 300 fits into this tradition (or the modern swords &amp; sandals permutation).<br /><br />However, when Miller is forced to give up some of his control, the improvement of realistic emotion shows how good his work can be. In <i>The Dark Knight Returns</i>, he had to keep much of the character's past and could not transform him entirely into an unfeeling, heroic killing machine. Likewise, in the film adaptation of <i>300</i>, the actors and director helped to infuse the characters with more emotion and depth.<br /><br />All in all, 300 isn't a long enough read for Miller's drawbacks to really hurt it, and he picked a fittingly manly story to showcase his histrionic machismo.<br /><br /><b>
  <a href="http://starsbeetlesandfools.blogspot.com/2013/09/suggested-readings-in-comics.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My Suggested Reading In Comics</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1576924985058794731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer241878181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14697042629399569264"><br/>Leonidas and his valiant band of about five thousand (300 Spartans, 3,100 Peloponnesians, and additional helots, Thespians, and Thebans) hold the pass at Thermopylae for as long as possible, but they receive no reinforcements and those who remain all die when Xerxes is shown a way around the pass. <br/><br/>Later Miller forgets about the 4700 guys who also died, tells a tale of great valor and sacrifice that will live on forever, never to be forgotten... Then a movie was made about the same. Then a joke.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8398760037082565602" style="display:none"><b>This is Sparta!</b><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554158792i/27301086._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>300 - a(master)piece of ancient Greece in pulp culture format!<br><br>Written and illustrated by Frank Miller, the classic battle of Thermopylae takes a new and modern dimension. A gritty and raw graphic novel that takes violence and comradeship into a whole new level.<br><br>Set in 480 BC, King Leonidas reunites the best 300 men at his disposal to fight the upcoming Persian invasion. King Xerxes (the Persian King), and his huge army will face the fury of these 300 fearless warriors at the narrow cliffs of the "Hot Gates" (Thermopylae). The Hot Gates will witness a scenario full of glory, and blood where retreating isn't part of the Spartans' plan. <br><br><b>An epic fictional retelling of the Battle of Thermopylae in a unique panorama.</b> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554159033i/27301094._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Rugged coloured scenes emphasizes the epic battles</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554159033i/27301095._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I remember a long time ago watching the adapted movie at the cinema, and thinking how epic it was! <br>In spite of the Historical inaccuracy in some aspects, the author grabs a Historical event and turns it into an epic story that highlights glory, sacrifice, and comradeship in a creative way.<br>Bold, imaginative, and daring, this short story has a solid flow throughout this Greek tale. <br><br><i>"Spartans... tonight we dine in Hell!"</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554158792i/27301089._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rating: 4.5/5 stars</span>

<div id="review_2618768162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2618768162" />
    <a title="L. McCoy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60482096-l-mccoy"><img alt="L. McCoy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528161175p2/60482096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2618768162?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L. McCoy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L. McCoy" href="/user/show/60482096-l-mccoy">L. McCoy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=comics-and-graphic-novels">comics-and-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=dark-horse">dark-horse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=creator-owned">creator-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=historic-fiction">historic-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618768162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6997996370853279832">I decided to read and review this since this is my 300th review on Goodreads! I never read this before, though I had seen the movie and like the movie, this isn’t bad though perhaps a tad overrated.<br/><br/>What’s it about?<br/>The spartans go at war with the Persians. <br/><br/>Pros:<br/>The story is fairly interesting if you like super dramatized war stories.<br/>The art is very well done.<br/>Lots of fantastic action scenes throughout. That is possibly the highlight of this comic. It’s super intense throughout.<br/>The dialogue is very</span>
  <span id="freeText6997996370853279832" style="display:none">I decided to read and review this since this is my 300th review on Goodreads! I never read this before, though I had seen the movie and like the movie, this isn’t bad though perhaps a tad overrated.<br /><br />What’s it about?<br />The spartans go at war with the Persians. <br /><br />Pros:<br />The story is fairly interesting if you like super dramatized war stories.<br />The art is very well done.<br />Lots of fantastic action scenes throughout. That is possibly the highlight of this comic. It’s super intense throughout.<br />The dialogue is very well written, I liked that a lot.<br /><br />Cons:<br />The story is rushed at times. <br />This book is slightly predictable, that may be because I’ve seen the movie before (the movie is very close to the source material) but still.<br />The lack of clothes annoyed me not because I give a fuck about nudity but because it’s cringey and historically inaccurate. The real spartans wore armor, in this they run around in a tore-up cape and underwear, I’m just confused by that. Also, there are several moments with characters just randomly walking around with their dicks out, don’t know why.<br />The ending’s super rushed and doesn’t even feel like an ending. Like, I half-wonder if Frank Miller had a deadline so he just sent his comic In without finishing it.<br /><br />Overall:<br />It’s okay but not all it’s hyped up to be. I liked the art, story and action but the ridiculous armor-less thing and not-an-ending make this only okay IMO.<br />If you’re a fan of the movie and haven’t read this then I’d recommend checking it out so you know the source material, otherwise there’s a lot of better comics to read.<br /><br />3/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="6997996370853279832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Dave  Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave  Johnson" href="/user/show/776528-dave-johnson">Dave  Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49111282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7927656131511351256">i saw the movie first and absolutely loved it, and after seeing it, i really wanted to read this. there's no real contrast between the two--they're virtually identical. but if you like graphic novels at all, this is a must-have. i have to say, rarely have i seen a graphic novel where the art takes center stage. sure there are comics with good art interspersed within the pages, but the art in this is just other-worldly. it's simply beautiful. <br/><br/>some of the complaints i've seen about this is that it</span>
  <span id="freeText7927656131511351256" style="display:none">i saw the movie first and absolutely loved it, and after seeing it, i really wanted to read this. there's no real contrast between the two--they're virtually identical. but if you like graphic novels at all, this is a must-have. i have to say, rarely have i seen a graphic novel where the art takes center stage. sure there are comics with good art interspersed within the pages, but the art in this is just other-worldly. it's simply beautiful. <br /><br />some of the complaints i've seen about this is that it's not true to history and that too much artistic license was taken on Miller's part. and i think that's funny considering that this is a comic, for chrissakes. this isnt supposed to be a historical documentary. this is, first and foremost, fiction. fiction based loosely on historical events with very little documentation. fiction meant to convey themes and ideals, not facts and data. like any great parable or allegory or story, this is more about the principle of the Spartans. it's about the tension between the valorous pride of the Spartans versus the hubris of the Persians; it's about the tension between freedom and slavery; it's about the price of freedom and the irony that the price of freedom is war; it's about bravery (of course) and why we admire people who sacrifice for others; and it's about loving freedom so much that you would give your life away just so your kids and country can still have it. <br /><br />it doesnt hurt that it looks pretty to boot.</span>

  <span id="freeText10654085147107815015" style="display:none">Frank Miller may be a talented comic book artist, but it should be understood that to align oneself with the Spartans in such a celebratory and narrow way as he has done is to be aligned with one of history's most oppressive and fascist states. Racism and "othering" are essential to his work, unfortunately, and the masses all too readily consume this entertaining "meal" unconsciously of the poison they have brought into their system.<br /><br />The historical inaccuracy of so many elements of the adaptation are truly laughable as well, but just the spectacle of Hoplites--heavy infantry--wearing "speedos" should be enough to give anyone who possesses a modicum of logic pause as to the historical validity of Miller's narrative.</span>

<div id="review_2731479825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2731479825" />
    <a title="Armand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45716474-armand"><img alt="Armand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591576251p2/45716474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2731479825?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Armand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Armand" href="/user/show/45716474-armand">Armand</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=ancient-world">ancient-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=archive">archive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2731479825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18274878985072952233">I understand that <i>300</i> took liberties with some historical details. The book talks about freedom and justice, but Sparta has a significant slave population. Waging a war virtually in the buff is an ill-advised idea, so our heroes fought with even more armor on them than the Persian horde. The Spartan rite of passage involves the hunting of not just a mere wolf, but involves targets that make the feat brutish and reprehensible, at least to us moderns. They deride Athenians as boy lovers though the</span>
  <span id="freeText18274878985072952233" style="display:none">I understand that <i>300</i> took liberties with some historical details. The book talks about freedom and justice, but Sparta has a significant slave population. Waging a war virtually in the buff is an ill-advised idea, so our heroes fought with even more armor on them than the Persian horde. The Spartan rite of passage involves the hunting of not just a mere wolf, but involves targets that make the feat brutish and reprehensible, at least to us moderns. They deride Athenians as boy lovers though they've been known to partake of those practices too. And so on and so forth.<br /><br />However, if I'm going to imbibe the tale in the spirit that Frank Miller intended, then yes, I have to say that the book has a very worthy story to tell. It reminds me of the celebrated songs of Homer - the ones that exalt the immortal feats of the heroes of the <i>Iliad</i> and the <i>Odyssey</i> - though in a less epic fashion. The narrator of the 300 is just a grizzled veteran of the campaign and not a notable rhapsodist of the Homeric tradition, but their function is the same. It is to instill the virtues that being a full-fledged warrior would require - courage, tenacity, strength, and cunning. Through this tale, one can anticipate the sacrifices that the rigors of war would exact. It regales its listeners with the glories that they shall enjoy should they acquit themselves honorably, with their actions and maybe even their names living on in ages to come, celebrated and lionized in aeternam. Thus with their death shall their immortality be realized.<br /><br />There are many things to savor in this book, a lot of memorable events and especially images. The wall made of rocks and the Persian dead. The bronzed temptation of Ephialtes. The magnificent gold-clad majesty of the divine emperor Xerxes. The image of a virile and strong army sleeping on the eve of the battle juxtaposed with - a few chapters later - a field strewn with the very same bodies, mercilessly arrow-pierced, lying faded in a more permanent slumber. <br /><br />It is smart too. I particularly liked how the young Leonidas's strategy against the wolf presaged the Hot Gates. <br /><br />I can't help but wonder how Miller managed to pack so much action in less than a hundred pages. It's one of the most inspiring pieces I've read this year, and even with its brevity it provides much to ponder. The ideas that it imparts seem very much apposite even now - <i>especially</i> now - in the soft, torpid springtime of a 21st century that's redolent with aimlessness and anomie.<br /><br />I'm rating this 8.5/10 or 4 epic stars out of 5. Looking forward to devouring its sequel, <i>Xerxes</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18274878985072952233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2695379241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2695379241" />
    <a title="Lee Conley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80185353-lee-conley"><img alt="Lee Conley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522683472p2/80185353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2695379241?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee Conley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee Conley" href="/user/show/80185353-lee-conley">Lee Conley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2695379241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11104053115444607786">A review of<br/>300<br/>by<br/>Frank Miller.<br/><br/>I’ll keep this brief, Spartan, you could say.<br/>I love Frank Miller’s work, and I decided to re-read and review his epic graphic novel 300. Its impact has not lessened from my first reading many years ago. <br/>In case you don’t know, it is the story of the battle of Thermopylae in Ancient Greece. We should all know the story; most of us have seen the excellent film. Three hundred kick-ass Spartan warriors stand against hordes of Persian invaders under the command of King Le</span>
  <span id="freeText11104053115444607786" style="display:none">A review of<br />300<br />by<br />Frank Miller.<br /><br />I’ll keep this brief, Spartan, you could say.<br />I love Frank Miller’s work, and I decided to re-read and review his epic graphic novel 300. Its impact has not lessened from my first reading many years ago. <br />In case you don’t know, it is the story of the battle of Thermopylae in Ancient Greece. We should all know the story; most of us have seen the excellent film. Three hundred kick-ass Spartan warriors stand against hordes of Persian invaders under the command of King Leonidas. They slaughter the Persians but are eventually overwhelmed and die to last man. We all know the story. But it’s Millers re-telling that makes this so special. The dialogue pulls no punches; it’s snappy and bad-ass. The art style is also on another level, and with the epic ancient story, it all combines to make a truly classic graphic novel. It’s an amazing modern re-telling of an epic story that has endured the ages and inspired us for thousands of years.<br />If you haven’t read it, and you enjoy graphic novels this is a must. The art is stunning, the writing makes you grimace and smile all at once. It’s simply BAD ASS.<br /><br />(In the words of Leonidas from the Film)<br />THIS IS SPARTA!<br /><br />Thanks for reading. <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14649012.Lee_C__Conley" title="Lee C. Conley" rel="nofollow noopener">Lee C. Conley</a></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AzXl3fnf5Xh3BT546xhKdrsNS7sad3e/3b6rurlDHwjyJiPoRDCC7dIBEwRWuFVJRNV7vaTihwHycg8s/khuJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rh83jbscrrh0kewW1ZB0kyyF1oSQc5i10NZ++1Arz/VfDPG4BvPJLdGVwWpoMGus013mgi7maAv/GtptFyC+2A==')})
  }
//]]>

We\'re in the most extreme and utter region of the human mind. A dim, subconscious underworld. A radiant abyss where men meet themselves. Hell, Netley. We\'re in Hell.&quot; \n\nHaving proved himself peerless in the arena of reinterpreting superheroes, Alan Moore turned his ever-incisive eye to the squalid, enigmatic world of Jack the Ripper and the Whitechapel murders of 1888. Weighing in at 576 pages, From Hell is certainly the most epic of Moore\'s works and remarkably and is possibly his finest effort yet in a career punctuated by such glorious highlights as Watchmen and V for Vendetta. Going beyond the myriad existing theories, which range from the sublime to the ridiculous, Moore presents an ingenious take on the slaughter. His Ripper\'s brutal activities are the epicentre of a conspiracy involving the very heart of the British Establishment, including the Freemasons and The Royal Family. A popular claim, which is transformed through Moore\'s exquisite and thoroughly gripping vision, of the Ripper crimes being the womb from which the 20th century, so enmeshed in the celebrity culture of violence, received its shocking, visceral birth. \n\nBolstered by meticulous research that encompasses a wide spectrum of Ripper studies and myths and coupled with his ability to evoke sympathies in such monstrous characters, Moore has created perhaps the finest examination of the Ripper legacy, observing far beyond society\'s obsessive need to expose Evil\'s visage. Ultimately, as Moore observes, Jack\'s identity and his actions are inconsequential to the manner in which society embraced the Fear: &quot;It\'s about us. It\'s about our minds and how they dance. Jack mirrors our hysterias. Faceless, he is the receptacle for each new social panic.&quot; \n\nEddie Campbell\'s stunning black and white artwork, replete with a scratchy, dirty sheen, is perfectly matched to the often-unshakeable intensity of Moore\'s writing. Between them, each murder is rendered in horrifying detail, providing the book\'s most unnerving scenes, made more so in uncomfortable, yet lyrical moments as when the villain embraces an eviscerated corpse, craving understanding; pleading that they &quot;are wed in legend, inextricable within eternity&quot;. \n\nThough technically a comic, the term hardly begins to describe From Hell\'s inimitable grandeur and finesse, as it takes the medium to fresh heights of ingenuity and craftsmanship. Moore and Campbell\'s autopsy on the emaciated corpse of the Ripper myth has divulged a deeply disturbing yet undeniably captivating masterpiece. —Danny Graydon<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer11381138976916224172">Frank Miller is an American writer, artist and film director best known for his film noir-style comic book stories. He is one of the most widely-recognized and popular creators in comics, and is one of the most influential comics creators of his generation. His most notable works include <i>Sin City, The Dark Knight Returns, Batman Year One</i> and <i>300</i>.<br/><br/><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11381138976916224172" style="display:none">Frank Miller is an American writer, artist and film director best known for his film noir-style comic book stories. He is one of the most widely-recognized and popular creators in comics, and is one of the most influential comics creators of his generation. But then, from the west, a tiger force strikes in Asia Minor and is on a course for collision with Persian forces.
